The Unification Church and the World
Every time we hold an official gathering, I always feel uncomfortable and sense that there are various barriers blocking us. Today, let’s talk freely. I believe there are many questions you want to ask me today, so let’s try to answer those questions. If you have a question, please raise your hand. Let’s be free… “I will ask a question.”

Question 1: The Secret to Your Health
Question: You always seem so healthy. Could you share the secret to your health? (laughter)
Answer: I was fortunate to be born to good parents and received good blood lineage, which has allowed me to be healthy. Currently, I weigh about 200 pounds, which is around 100 kilograms. Even during my time in prison, while enduring the hardships of imprisonment in Hungnam, I maintained a weight of 190 pounds. I have a sturdy build and I believe this is due to the legacy my ancestors left me. Additionally, as I have engaged in various activities, I had to ensure my own safety. Therefore, I did not miss out on any exercise in my twenties. Because I exercised, I learned how to treat my body whenever something was wrong, which is how I maintain my health today. I have a method of exercising. I wish I could teach it all to you, but there isn’t enough time. (laughs) 

Furthermore, there is also a mental belief. When I go to high places, I don’t think of them as high, and when I go to low places, I don’t think of them as low. I maintain an ordinary mental stability. That’s a difficult concept. What is this mental stability? No matter how complex or difficult the problem is… even after going through life for over 60 years… I have walked a history of struggle throughout my life. During the Japanese colonial period, I fought against the colonial authorities and lived in prison at that time. I also lived in prison in North Korea, in South Korea, and now I am destined to live in prison in America as well. 

But it doesn’t end there. The standard we are heading towards is to go through China and reach Moscow. This is how I see it. The departure for that journey is not merely crossing a river. It involves crossing vast and wide oceans, and having the criteria to go beyond continents. We must establish a mental stability to prepare for that. 

Then, that becomes another question. How do we achieve that? It is through faith. If there is an absolute being, there must be a relationship between that absolute being and myself… There must be a place where that absolute being can be stable. If we can participate in that stable place, it becomes possible. This may sound difficult. If God exists, He must be positioned somewhere. If He governs through the history of the human world or through religious foundations, there must be a basis for that governance, and that basis would be the stable point that God desires on earth. If we are in that stable point, even though we may be weak, when we face the grand purpose of providence, we can follow a stable path, which is why I consider that path stable. It’s a difficult concept. 

Next, what about…? 

Question 2: How Do You Make Decisions? (Prayer, Revelation, Yourself)
Question: I am Professor Lee Gi-ok from Hanyang University. It seems you make very macro and exceptional decisions every time. When you make those decisions, do you receive answers through prayer, receive revelations, or do you decide for yourself? I would like to know a bit about that. 
Answer: There are various aspects to this. I have my own antenna and my own dial. What does that mean? It could be called revelation. When I meet people, I can understand. I was born with a certain disposition. This is a past story, but from the age of seven or eight, I was known in my neighborhood or town as someone who could arrange marriages based on photographs. Do you understand what I mean? If I looked at a photo and said “good” or “bad,” it would turn out that way. There is something like that, an intuition. When I enter a neighborhood, I already get a premonition. If I think, “Something will happen in this neighborhood,” it usually happens within a week; I was born with such a talent. 

Therefore, when I go to America, I can intuitively judge the situation there. I can say, “This country will face a crisis at some point,” and it turns out to be true. The content is complex. It is a religious issue, and the stages that can be reached through the process of cultivation are quite complicated. However, it is something that anyone can achieve. Of course, being born with a religious disposition may be a reason, but there is also a path that can be reached through human cultivation. The Unification Church knows this. It understands this and knows this taste. 

Currently, missionaries are going out to various countries, but they are going alone. They endure persecution and hardship for seven years, yet they can see what will happen tomorrow. They already know in advance through inspiration. This is a spiritual secret that no one in the Unification Church can explain, but it is possible. 

Therefore, the facts experienced are more certain than any other fact, and the facts that are denied are below the certain standards that one feels. When this happens, anyone can overcome their environment and the path of persecution. 

The conclusion is this. If it is spiritual, it is spiritual, and there are things that can be seen and felt in revelation. Therefore, I believe that this is how I can make such significant decisions and take such actions. Among the things I have done over the years, there are things that I have aimed for and decided upon for 30 to 40 years. I often feel that I am still moving forward with those decisions. That may be due to some relationship with God, if God exists. Do you understand? That world is completely unknown. 

Next, is there anyone else with a question? 

Question 3: What Do You Think Will Happen to North Korean Communism in the Future?
Question: I am a professor at Korea University. From a global perspective, what do you think will happen to North Korean communism in the future? 
Answer: As long as God exists, I believe communism will disappear. That is why I am currently fighting at the forefront of the world. The position that Rev. Moon occupies now is that of a person of interest to the CIA in the United States. The FBI reports to higher authorities about me daily. When the changes in the future world situation evolve in ways we cannot imagine, I believe there are many paths for the KGB of the Soviet Union and the CIA of the United States to negotiate. 

So, when you look at the Kremlin, the KGB of the Soviet Union, and Moscow, Rev. Moon is the greatest enemy that has appeared throughout the history of communism from its inception to now. But he is not an ignorant enemy. He has already been proven to be an extremely intelligent enemy. 

How is that proven? Japan has a political system centered on liberalization, and within that environment, Rev. Moon has emerged and completely blocked the path of the Japanese Communist Party. 

As you all know, I have cut off the heads of mayors from Kyoto to Nagoya, Osaka, and even the mayor of Minobe in Tokyo. I eliminated two-thirds of the 180 liberal mayors. How did I do that? That’s the mystery. The results are evident, but how it happened is something you wouldn’t know unless you ask me. 

From this perspective, communism is now facing Rev. Moon… it’s not about President Reagan. It’s not about any leader of an anti-communist country. Rev. Moon has emerged as a figure in the world problem. That is why the United States is watching me from that perspective. 

Just looking at this trial case, the plaintiff is the United States of America. It is not a department or the Ministry of Justice. The United States of America vs. Defendant Rev. Moon. This is the fight. Ultimately, it is a battle between the United States, the leading country of the free world, and Rev. Moon alone. 

There have been many difficulties in this process, but now we are at the final critical point, facing a situation that could cause confusion in administrative law. I cannot disclose that now. If this is resolved, it could become a historically shining victory for the Unification Church. I believe that with the conclusion of this case, the era of opposition for the Unification Church will pass. 

To resolve this case, the United States has mobilized 25 countries through the State Department and all investigative agencies behind it. They have mobilized embassies from 25 countries, and through their intelligence networks and the intelligence agents of the countries involved, they have been working to cut this off decisively. However, this issue is now heading in an unusual direction and is in a very dangerous stage. 

I believe the situation will improve, but the KGB and the CIA have entered a stage where they can negotiate politically around Rev. Moon. I have already received reports about this. This is through a third country… 

From this position, I am moving forward. However, no matter what they do, communism is destined to perish. And the activities of communism are such. Of course, since you are professors, you understand communism well, but if we take Japan as an example, where has the Communist Party found a base to develop rapidly until now? It is in the universities. In the universities, smart professors, especially those specializing in economics… communism is a philosophy of economics. 

Smart professors should rally their students, but they absolutely do not do so using communist theories. Instead, they use other indirect events or attack someone, representing something unfavorable to society, and the professors take responsibility for that. 

Then, the attacked side defends itself and counterattacks. This creates a public opinion in society, and they execute a strategy that corners themselves. This is just one example. When students see that their teacher is a well-respected professor in the school, with a history of being praised in all aspects of teaching, and they see him being countered by society, they think it is unacceptable. 

Having created such an environment, they call their students and appeal to them. “Look, in this environment, you must help me. This impure environment arises from the foundation of capitalism,” they fundamentally criticize communism. 

As they explain this, ultimately the students end up siding with the teacher, and they are secretly educated without realizing it. As they educate, they are exposed to a worldview they have never heard before. “Now, you gather your friends at school,” they say, and the professor takes responsibility to present his beloved students… It doesn’t have to be a large number. If it’s just 10 or 20, they distribute leaflets… They are trained for this. They are exceptionally trained to mobilize the entire group. 

They use these students to distribute leaflets and incite demonstrations. When demonstrations occur, who responds? It is the labor unions, the labor unions. In Japan, all newspapers, including Yomiuri, Asahi, and Mainichi, are aligned with the liberal camp. Why? Because there are labor unions. The labor unions threaten the printing houses when they print. “This is the root of capitalism, this is the institution that exploits us, and this newspaper is pushing the Japanese nation into being our enemy, so we must print from the perspective of the workers!” they command through their leaders in a coordinated manner. 

Having done this, they create situations that force people to listen to them. As a result, they manipulate the workers and create such a situation, and so on. (The recording briefly cuts out) 

So, I opened all the doors and laid the groundwork, secretly teaching the students martial arts. I thought, “These kids cannot be allowed to continue.” At Tokyo University, there is a communist festival called May Day on May 1st. During this period, we also held a large anti-communist rally. This was a life-or-death situation. Tokyo University and Waseda University are large universities, and they were preparing to celebrate the communist May Day, intending to take over the entire school, but opposition forces emerged, so they could not just sit back. It was a direct confrontation. They were called out. 

In this way, the smallest and most skilled individuals went out and defeated the communists. We fought like this. 

Therefore, the communists cannot defeat us through violence, martial arts, theory, or organizational strength. They think that if they do not meet us on the stage where intellectuals gather, everything will be resolved, but that itself is already a retreat. 

As a result, the Japanese Communist Party, which boasted more than 150,000 members from Tokyo University, had only about 400 members at the last convention. The president of the Principle Research Association reported to me that the communists are becoming miserable. So, he asked for some support from behind. “If they disappear completely, the right-wing parties will rise, you know!” I have said such things. 

Looking at such examples, I believe that as long as the Unification Church exists, communism will disappear. Do you understand? 

Next, what about…? 

Question 4: The Future of Korea, Korea's Position, and the Future of Human Culture.
Question: Many people say that the work you have done globally until now is something that ordinary humans cannot achieve, and that it is possible because of God's power or some other spiritual force. Another thing I've heard, although I haven't seen it myself, is that when Unification Church members from abroad come to Korea, they kiss the ground as soon as they land at Gimpo Airport. I heard they do this because it is the birthplace of our leader, Reverend Moon. When foreigners ask me about this, I say I don't know much about the principles of the Unification Church and haven't studied it deeply, so I can't answer well. I would like to ask this question indirectly. 

That is, you are doing so many projects, and I believe that God's will is being fulfilled through you, but I wonder what kind of occasion or revelation leads to this. 

Another point is that about 25 years ago, when I was in college, I had the opportunity to meet Professor Toynbee directly. At that time, he mentioned that the future culture of humanity would not come from Europe but would emerge from the East, becoming the center of world culture. Considering this, you were born in Korea. Among the various reports I heard earlier, you have accomplished many things that are truly almost impossible for ordinary humans. I would like to hear your thoughts on Korea's future, Korea's position, and how human culture will evolve in relation to the world.

Answer: This issue requires us to delve into world history, and it will be a vast topic. If you understand the principles of the Unification Church and its background, you will come to know God's providence. God's providence. You will understand how God has laid bridges through religions in the historical process, connecting religions to culture, and how all phenomena in society—including economic and political issues—are woven together around a grand purpose that we humans do not know.

This is how it is woven together, but people do not understand this. Religious people cannot see the entirety of religion, and politicians act for their own interests and ambitions, but ultimately, they are all operating within the realm of providence of the great universe.

When we look at politicians, they stand on a historical path, but they do not understand it. They always want to achieve more and extend their political life, but they often encounter misfortune and break apart. This leads not only to the downfall of individuals but also to the collapse of parties and nations.

No one desires this. Who would want such a thing? The fact that unwanted events occur frequently raises the question of why this happens. To put it simply, it sounds like a mundane topic, but it is a strange story. People often say, "Today is my lucky day!" Dr. Yun probably uses such expressions occasionally. "Ah, today was lucky!" they might say.

What exactly is luck? Such expressions are used by individuals and even among friends. In families, people say, "Our family is lucky! Our company had good fortune!" When South Korea competes in a soccer match at an Asian tournament and wins against a technically superior opponent, they say, "Our team was lucky!" This sentiment also applies when a nation engages in diplomacy. Even in the political arena where the democratic world and the communist world confront each other, such expressions are valid.

This indicates that all humans in this historical era are being drawn into this process, regardless of whether they are religious or non-religious. 

For example, take South Korea. Wouldn't you wish for South Korea not to collapse? That is a wish. We hope it does not collapse, but it cannot collapse... Kim Il-sung also says, "Oh, we must not collapse." Whether he invades South Korea or seeks unification, he thinks of himself as a great man who can influence from Manchuria to China.

Therefore, along with the expansion of the pro-North Korean faction in Japan, they are now reaching out to the Korean diaspora in the United States. North Korea has its own thoughts, and South Korea has its own. This is how conflicts arise. The question is, what happens when conflicts occur?

There are national fortunes and global fortunes; there is the fortune of the world and the fortune of heaven. In such cases, who is the wise person? It is someone who has unknowingly made decisions that align with heavenly fortune. When that happens, a nation may be in a position to collapse, but a path for survival can emerge. This is why leaders are needed.

In the past, looking at Judaism, the prophets often advised rulers. Regarding the Carter administration... that rat-like Carter. I once referred to the representative of the U.S. government, which leads the free world, as "that son of a bitch Carter" in public. I did not say this out of ignorance. It was disrespectful to the nation and to the free world... I know that anyone, foreign or domestic, should maintain decorum towards their country, but I felt this was unacceptable. From the day he was elected, I declared war publicly and attacked every day for four years. "FBI, CIA, speak up! I, Reverend Moon, may be ridiculed and criticized in the U.S., but my words will be recorded in the historical declaration of Congress. Report it!" I have been doing this.

I currently have all the confidential documents that were sent to the South Korean embassy. Looking back... Koreans need to wake up. I won't go into detail about these political matters, but the conclusion is that President Carter himself sent a public document to the embassy stating, "Reverend Moon is our political enemy." "He is our enemy! Let's take him down!" That is what was conveyed. Knowing this, they thought, "Let's see who breaks first, you or me."

Thus, in supporting President Reagan, Mr. Park promised more than a million votes. At that time, the Republican Party had surrendered New York to the Democrats and locked up their offices. New York, Pennsylvania with Philadelphia, and Massachusetts with Harvard University were all strongholds of the Democrats. This was all under the influence of Senator Edward. Then Connecticut, and then Minnesota with Congressman Fraser—these five states were all abandoned by the Republicans. We went out and turned everything upside down. This has become a hidden story in modern political history, a secret topic. How did we do it? You don't know, do you? We did it.

These days, there is a lot of fuss about the New York gubernatorial election and various mayoral elections. So I joked, "If you want to be the mayor, come visit our East Garden!" I think they will come if invited. Our newspaper has a news world in New York City. There is Noticia del Mundo, and the Spanish-speaking population is close to three million. They are extremely weak in terms of votes. If you spit in your palm and say, "I will vote for you, so lick the spit off my palm," they will do it. There are anecdotes behind this.

So why do we engage in such struggles? I know I will be persecuted, so why do I do it? I know I will suffer losses. I do it for the future of South Korea. That is the purpose.

I am currently engaged in many activities. Now, even world-renowned scholars, whether they have won Nobel Prizes or not, wait two hours to meet me, and they cannot complain if I do not meet them. I have created such an environment. 

What I am about to do is to establish a cultural revolution based on absolute values. For over ten years, I have been holding scientific conferences, but now I need to lay the groundwork for a cultural revolution. Encyclopedias and all dictionaries differ... Buddhist countries are different, and communist countries have completely new concepts and lack religious concepts. Even in the current democratic world, the understanding of God is vague. 

As a result, how many young people of the second generation are suffering? Someone must draw the line. If scientists gather, world-renowned scientists must study and prove that God certainly exists. If they cannot, they must at least acknowledge it in some way. We must establish a new starting point centered on God as the standard of absolute value; otherwise, the survival of the world depends on it.

To achieve this, I am working on a 12-year plan. We have already held eleven conferences. Now, as we conclude the twelfth conference, we must make a real start, and this is a vast plan. We will organize all encyclopedias around this and create a cultural environment that can aim for a unified world for future generations. This is a massive undertaking. It sounds like a dream, but now we have entered the realm of possibility. 

We have established a foundation that can gather 100,000 world-renowned masters or professors from various fields. This is truly remarkable. 

So whenever we hold such gatherings, I always worry that distinguished professors in Korea can take the lead on this stage, but the question is who will do it. Since I am Korean, I would like to see Korean professors take the lead. However, to do that, there must be a foundation of Korean scholars that can gain the trust of professors worldwide, who have established practical achievements that no one in any academic field can follow. Without that, it cannot be done.

Now, all of this is about saving Korea. That is what I am saying. Last year, while holding the scientific conference, I knew that the Korean government did not welcome me as I am currently engaged in legal battles. But why? This scientific conference was not held for propaganda purposes. It is to save the Republic of Korea, connecting with professors.

If you had not published four books last year, I would have been very embarrassed. You all worked hard, but the foundation has already been established around Reverend Moon, centered on unification thought or the Unification Theological Seminary, with dozens of books already published. In the future, if opposing individuals or journalists do not acknowledge this and continue to oppose, the academic world will call the journalists and give them a hard time. They are all my disciples.

Considering that we are moving into such an environment, why do we engage in such struggles? It is to defend the Republic of Korea. We are creating bases to defend against communism in the United States, Japan... There is only one way for the Republic of Korea to survive. I believe there is only one way. Now, unification between Kim Il-sung and the South Korean government will not happen. It absolutely will not happen. Look. There is a different constitution in China. There is the Soviet Union. And there is Japan. Japan is at a stage where it dreams of a return to imperialism, centered on its economic kingdom, and is opposing U.S. policy. Then, the U.S. has also become involved in this. Surviving in the midst of these four great powers is absolutely impossible for Korea alone. Reverend Moon is already thinking this way.

Therefore, the question is who to draw in? Who to push into this? China cannot do it. The Soviet Union cannot do it either because it is a communist party. We must understand the nature of that communist party. It has already concluded theoretically that it will overthrow capitalism and dominate the world. To achieve this, it does not care about means and methods. Therefore, the Soviet Union and the communist party can unite and divide whenever their sovereignty is threatened. We must see this. They cannot be considered enemies. Even when they are in opposition, if a stronger enemy appears, they will always unite. This is the strategy of the communist party.

From this perspective, the unification of North and South Korea... do they conduct elections as they please? Recently, I have heard reports that Kim Jong-il has made various compromises with China, but I hear this through intelligence agencies.

Behind all these movements, there are ultimately the mother countries. If we look at it this way, the mother country of North Korea could be China or the Soviet Union. Korea is also a small nation, so it has a mother country. In the past, Japan was the mother country, but now it is dependent on the United States. It is dependent on the United States. The Americans may retreat at any time.

For example, if there is a way to absorb China, then Korea could be given up at any time. Do you understand what I mean? If the U.S. finds a way to absorb China, Korea could be handed over to Kim Il-sung or the Soviet Union. It could be handed over to China. I believe this could happen without a fight. Korea is in a position where it could be sold at any time. No matter how much you dislike it, what can you do? In the past, did any black people want to be sold in the white market? The sorrow of the weak is that they cannot help it.

The reason I went abroad is also that. Currently, Japan is not a Christian nation. It is a nation of mixed religions, a hybrid religion. They believe in everything from the eight million gods to the heads of cod. It is a nation of mixed religious authority. And the United States stands within the Christian cultural sphere. They do not match in terms of constitution.

In the future, as Japan becomes one with the United States, of course, they will follow the free world line, but there are many heterogeneous elements. When national interests are at stake, the content will change at any time.

So how do we bind Japan to the United States? This has been my thought until now. After liberation, when all citizens were shouting "Long live independence," I could not shout "Long live independence." Given Korea's geopolitical environment, I believed that without leaping beyond the four great powers, there would be no way to survive, which is why I could not shout.

I thought I had to start on my own. 

Having done that, what am I doing now? What is the Unification Church doing? It has entered the realm of a different religious sphere in Japan and is conducting a movement for the ideological transformation of Christianity. Now, I have laid a considerable foundation. I have created an environment that cannot be touched by the political circles of Japan. 

To go through such a process, I have had many hardships behind the scenes. I am a religious person, and meeting prominent politicians in Japan has been challenging due to the opposition I face. I had to send people to connect with the elders of the Liberal Democratic Party... Was it in 1978 when I held a banquet in Japan? "It was 1975." Then how many years ago was that? Seven years ago. At that time, I held a banquet at the Imperial Hotel, where about 1,700 of the most prominent people from across the country gathered. There, former Prime Minister Kishi Nobusuke became the executive chairman. Do you understand what that means? Former Prime Minister Kishi introduced Reverend Moon at the banquet.
I became the executive chairman. 
While that sounds simple, the history behind it is filled with many painful stories. It could fill several books. It involves everything from governors to prime ministers... At that time, the brothers were fighting among themselves. I have many anecdotes starting from the work of reconciliation. 

In Korea, there were rumors that a certain Moon was a colorless man who was running away after abducting a married woman, while no one knew about my meetings with high-ranking officials in Japanese politics. During the banquet, former Prime Minister Fukuda was supposed to introduce me in his speech. At that time, the Minister of Defense, Ogura Daijin, had gathered representatives of the national emergency economic policy to hold a meeting on national policy and economic issues, which coincided with our meeting. So, there was an incident where former Prime Minister Fukuda interrupted his meeting to come and give a speech. At that banquet, he spoke of me as a great figure in Asia, but I was met with strong rebuttals from the communists. 

Now, I have been intertwined with such games up to this point. I have now established a considerable foundation. I have been involved with the Self-Defense Forces and their internal staff for the past 15 years, running around. 

Currently, the Liberal Democratic Party is centered around the elders, and what issues have arisen? They are trying to pull Japan out of the Liberal Democratic Party, but there is no middle class that can connect the elders with the youth. How do we fill this gap? This is what we are struggling with now. We are entering an era of political change, with figures like Nakasone and Fukuda emerging, but once this era passes, it will become quite difficult. That is why the elders of the Japanese government have great trust in us. They say, "You must be the ones," and it has become clear that you have won a decisive victory. We have now reached such a stage. 

Therefore, based on this political climate, I proposed a spy law seven years ago, believing that we must organize a national organization. There is a famous lawyer in Tokyo named Ogata, who is the president of the Tokyo Bar Association. I persuaded him to visit five advanced countries. I coached him on this spy law entirely. Now, there is a struggle in the National Assembly to pass this spy law. 

So, there has been a reorganization of local Liberal Democratic Party members. We cannot just leave it as it is. We need to arm ourselves ideologically. Now, we have entered the educational phase centered around the Victory and Alliance. Along with these grassroots activities... 

When looking at Japan and Korea, Japan's ancestors are Korea, right? The culture centered around Baekje has all been inherited, leading to modern Japan. How can these children, who do not recognize their ancestors, speak so loudly? Therefore, we need to educate them about their ancestors, and recently, we have been bringing 350 people every month to the Little Angels Hall for education. Now, we need to bring two teams, four teams each month for education. This is the movement we are undertaking. By expanding this grassroots base, we need to intertwine the economic and political sectors and place a Christian ideological cultural cap on it. 

Why is that? Because this is how we can connect with the United States on a national scale. Currently, the policy directions of the United States and Japan are different. 

At this time, the Soviet Union and China are competing fiercely, and the country that will ultimately achieve victory in the struggle against capitalism alongside Asian dominance will be the communist world. Therefore, China must dominate Asia in its own way, and the Soviet Union must do so in its own way. 

However, the good news is that there are 3.2 billion people living in Asia. And the Soviet Union is a white nation. From a geographical perspective, they are at a disadvantage. Nevertheless, in military and political fields, the Soviet Union currently surpasses China. Therefore, the Soviet Union believes that if it can swallow Japan, it will take the lead in the future confrontation with the United States centered around the Pacific stage. 

Based on this environment, the current issue of Deng Xiaoping dancing equally with the United States and various underlying identity issues are intertwined. China also wants to connect with Japan. Through Kim Il-sung, they are trying to push down and secure South Korea. This place is a complete fortress, so if they can control it, they believe Japan will fall into their hands. The Soviet Union thinks the same way. 

If Japan and Kim Il-sung become one, what will happen to the Soviet Union? They will cast their net in Korea. Political experts know well that casting a net can lead to difficulties. Korea could be sold off without realizing it. If that happens, the United States will be pulled out. 

Currently, Korea is divided into North and South, but if a division between East and West occurs, Japan will enter the Soviet sphere without a fight. 

For example, if we talk about Hokkaido... the area around Alaska is a globally renowned fishing ground. To fish in Hokkaido, one must obtain approval from the Hokkaido Fisheries Association, and to cross territorial waters, one must receive approval from the Soviet Union due to the 200-mile issue. There is no Japanese strait. Under these conditions, they are already within the Soviet sphere of influence. 

Now, if that happens, the Soviet Union will take the entire Korean Peninsula without a fight. Why? Because they are based in the Indian Ocean, embracing India and passing through Indochina to Taiwan... The leader of Taiwan, Jiang Jingguo, is a graduate of a Soviet university. So, centered around the Korean Peninsula and the East Coast, Japan will be automatically surrounded. If that happens, Japan will have nowhere to go. 

Under these conditions, we must connect with the United States before that time comes. We need to engage in a youth movement in the United States alongside the second Christianization... We need to mobilize Christianity, but this Christianity is opposing us. I expect this trial to last until a year and a half to two years, until 1983. At the latest, until 1984, I believe we will pass the era of persecution against the Unification Church. 

Currently, the youth in America have no way forward. They are already exhausted from the democratic world system. They are tired of the Christian cultural sphere. They have not even considered this. Until now, they have been exhausted from rampaging against communism. They are now in this buffer zone.

What will happen with the interdenominational movement? By creating one church and cooperating with each other, rather than one person's claim, ten people can come together, combine their efforts, and pray sincerely, and then all the paths will be known.

Therefore, for Christianity to go in one direction, it must inevitably lay a bridge in the last days. But how should that bridge be laid? It cannot be done with the ideas that have been asserted and lived within the 20th century. It cannot be done. It has already been tested. The democratic world has been tested, and the communist world has been tested. Communism emerged from a theological and religious foundation. It has all been tested. 

Now, this world is undergoing constant and unpredictable changes. Unless we can digest this and establish an ideological foundation that can take a leading role in it, we will fall behind. We will be eliminated. The distance will grow further and further. It is getting further away. So who will follow that world that is getting further away? The youth? Not a chance.

Therefore, we have moved past the era of conceptual religion and now need an existential God who can lead in empirical and practical aspects. Only those who can walk a smooth path based on that principle under God's guidance will remain in the end. In that sense, even though the Unification Church is criticized... I am speaking for myself. When I look at myself, am I just being criticized? I do not engage in this for the sake of being a fertilizer.

I must bring strong and courageous young people to fulfill God's will. Look, I have faced so much persecution until now. Whether during the Liberal Party, the Democratic Party, or the Communist Party, I have faced opposition for 37 years from Christianity. Yet, despite that opposition, I have grown this much. Now, there is a great wave in American universities called "Munism." In South America, they are now trying to bring me over to their countries.
Competition is heating up. It's all a fact that sounds like a lie. "That Moon, whoever he is, can lie well in that position!" If someone thinks it's a lie, let them think so. They are either a sleepyhead who knows nothing about the world or a crazy person. This is what's happening.

Look. Young people in America are bound to go through the Unification Church at some point. "Mr. Moon is the greatest person in the world. Let's all go!" At that time, when I hold a revival meeting, they will be swept away. Even when there was opposition, when I held lectures, all the major venues in America, like the Washington Monument, were packed. So, what do you think will happen to the Unification Church when that time comes? It will be a big deal. What will happen if you oppose it then? Even if I stay quiet, will the young guys, those vigorous college students, just sit still after hearing bad things? They will speak up or make a fuss. They will do it even without me telling them. And then they will report to me, "Teacher, can we survive with a young temperament? Teacher, do you want dead students, or do you want lively, strong, and bold students?" When I say, "I want strong and bold students!" they will say, "Then please shut your mouth!" What will happen then? If I say I couldn't do it, they will scoff at me. (Laughter) It's not a laughing matter. It sounds like a half-threat, but it would be better to take it to heart even if you feel hurt. Do you understand?

Here, to the evangelists and ladies from some church! Be strong and bold. And to the elders... I really don't like the term elder. Why do we call them elders? We should call them young elders. Because they are elders, they are useless. What can you do when you're old? I will change the name of the established church. Don't call them elders; call them young elders. Is there any better word than "young"? Who likes old people? I am old too, but I am trying to imitate the young. Even though I am over 60, I sweat while... guiding the young, so I naturally became like this.

It shouldn't be disrespectful to the older teachers and elder brothers, but even if it shouldn't be, it can't be helped. I need to vent a little. If I can't vent to you, if I can't let it out to those close to me, I will die. (Laughter) I know I shouldn't die, right? Even if I curse, I shouldn't die. I need to stay alive, right? There is so much to do. "You must live until the 21st century." Ah! That's the curse I hate the most. I know the spirit world well, and if I go now, there is so much to do. Moreover, what interesting wind has blown in Japan? You all heard about the joint wedding ceremony, right? Who led that? It was this ugly man here, a Korean. What wind has blown in Japan? To get married in Japan, you need to bring 100 million yen. The middle class and upper class need to have 100 million yen. However, for the joint wedding ceremony, it only cost 50,000 yen. Do you know what 50,000 yen is? In our Korean currency, with the current exchange rate, it's less than 140,000 won. They even had money left after the wedding. Do you understand?

Young guys in Japan, students who are studying abroad, are smart. When those students want to get married, it's a big deal. That's why even if they say not to join the Unification Church, they still come in. And when I ask the young people who are holding the steering wheel in Korea, "Are you married?" they say, "No, I haven't married." "Then you should get married!" "Oh, who would come to marry me?" they say. "Why not? If there are young guys, they should come to marry, right? Why not?" Then they say, "What do you mean why not? These days, all the girls are melting into Japanese guys and Western guys. Oh, there are only trash cans left." And they say, "Oh, I don't like that, but still, there is no one who says they would come!" Why is that? Because to get married, you need at least 10 million won. That's the reality.

Even if you can't do it, you have to buy the bride's dress. You have to get the groom's suit and shoes. Then you have to decorate the wedding room. There is nothing like not meeting for 40 days like in the Unification Church. You have to meet right away. When you meet, relatives, in-laws, and everyone come and say you have to treat them. Even with 10 million won, it's not enough. I have heard from many people. Where else can you find such a good deal?" (Laughter) Now that the atmosphere has become like this, I say, "That's good," so let's try it.
